45:1070:86420:14:28:72:527:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Frank Lloyd Wright began his career as an architect in 1887, at the age of 20. Over the 
45:1071:86508:28:27:71:524:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:course of the next 72 years he produced designs for more than 1000 buildings, of which more 
45:1072:86600:27:28:71:514:133:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:than 400 were constructed. No single building has clearly emerged as his greatest work, but 
45:1073:86692:28:0:71:519:105:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:among those that have received the greatest attention is Fallingwater, a house Wright built at 
46:1074:86790:0:27:72:523:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Bear Run, Pennsylvania, in 1937, when he was 70 years old. When the house was completed, 
46:1075:86879:27:28:72:522:657:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f4:Time featured Wright on its cover, with a drawing of the house behind him - the first time the 
46:1076:86974:28:27:72:524:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:magazine had an architect on its cover.199 A recent survey of American architecture described 
46:1077:87068:27:28:72:543:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Fallingwater as “Wright’s most famous building of all,” and a leading architectural scholar called 
46:1078:87167:28:28:72:386:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:it “one of the complete masterpieces of twentieth-century art.”200 
46:1079:87233:28:27:72:506:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Early in his career Wright formulated a set of propositions to define his concept of 
46:1080:87318:27:28:72:521:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:organic architecture, which “evolved from a set of architectural principles in the 1890s into a 
46:1081:87414:28:27:72:524:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:lifestyle by the 1930s.”201 These principles emphasized the importance of simplicity of form,  
46:1082:87509:27:28:72:541:464:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:harmony between a building and its natural setting,  the use of natural colors, and using materials 
46:1083:87609:28:28:72:518:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:to express their own nature rather than imitating other materials. Wright wanted buildings to 
46:1084:87703:28:27:72:491:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:share the human virtues of sincerity, truthfulness, and graciousness. Within these basic 
46:1085:87792:27:28:72:541:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:guidelines Wright developed distinctively new architectural forms, which never ceased to change 
46:1086:87888:28:27:72:540:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:as he continually experimented throughout his long career. Yet Wright’s style evolved gradually, 
46:1087:87985:27:28:72:543:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:and a recent survey concluded that “when we look at the totality of his oeuvre, we see in his form 
46:1088:88084:28:27:72:433:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:language a remarkable coherence, continuity, and recurrence of motifs.”202 
46:1089:88158:27:28:72:508:271:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: By 1900, Wright had developed his celebrated Prairie Style. Its distinctive features 
46:1090:88243:28:28:72:520:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:included an emphasis on long horizontal lines, relating its buildings to the open spaces of the 
46:1091:88339:28:27:72:500:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Midwestern plains, and a blurring of the distinction between interior and exterior spaces, 
46:1092:88430:27:28:72:519:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:achieved through covered but open areas around a building’s perimeter.203 Over time Wright 
46:1093:88521:28:27:72:520:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:continued to experiment and to simplify the style, and the most famous of the Prairie houses, 
46:1094:88615:27:28:72:309:133:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Chicago’s Robie House, was completed in 1910. 
46:1095:88661:28:0:72:519:105:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Wright’s experimental approach is revealed not only in the continual evolution of his 
47:1096:88750:0:27:72:529:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:style but also in his reluctance to determine his buildings’ final forms. He advised architects to 
47:1097:88849:27:28:71:205:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:let their ideas grow slowly: 
47:1098:88878:28:14:143:457:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Conceive the building in the imagination, not on paper but in the 
47:1099:88944:14:13:143:438:615:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:mind... Let it live there - gradually taking more definite form 
47:1100:89008:13:14:143:466:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:before committing it to the draughting board. When the thing lives 
47:1101:89075:14:14:143:452:588:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:for you - start to plan it with tools... Working on it with triangle 
47:1102:89144:14:14:143:438:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:and T-square should modify or extend or intensify or test the 
47:1103:89206:14:14:143:214:560:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:conception.204 
47:1104:89220:14:13:144:147:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: 
47:1105:89220:13:28:72:540:533:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:During the time the design was taking shape, or “germinating,” Wright needed to have its setting 
47:1106:89317:28:28:71:492:505:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:firmly in mind: “A building should appear to grow easily from its site and be shaped to 
47:1107:89405:28:27:72:524:477:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:harmonize with its surroundings.”205 Wright not only avoided committing himself to plans on 
47:1108:89497:27:28:72:537:450:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:paper as long as possible, but he typically made changes in his projects until the actual materials 
47:1109:89597:28:27:72:543:422:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:were set in place, and sometimes even after. A biographer observed that “his impromptu methods 
47:1110:89692:27:28:72:528:395:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:of designing, which led to his continual failure to prepare complete working drawings, made it 
47:1111:89787:28:28:72:535:367:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:necessary for him to be on the site as often as possible during the time that a building was under 
47:1112:89886:28:27:72:528:339:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:construction.” Although this annoyed many builders, and dismayed many clients as alterations 
47:1113:89979:27:28:72:489:312:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:during construction raised their costs, it never fazed Wright, for “to him the process of 
47:1114:90069:28:27:72:534:284:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:construction was a process of refinement as well.”206 A former student of Wright’s recalled that 
47:1115:90166:27:28:72:519:257:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:“he always changed everything. A perpetual state of flux. ‘The last change is made when the 
47:1116:90258:28:27:72:514:229:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:boom comes down,’ he’d snort.”207 Wright explained his attitude more gently when a client 
47:1117:90348:27:28:72:520:202:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:complained to him of the delays, and expenses, that resulted from Wright’s constant changes 
47:1118:90440:28:28:72:532:174:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:during the construction of one of his most important projects: “You see the building grows as it 
47:1119:90537:28:27:72:394:146:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:is built and is none too easy, therefore, to keep up with always.”208 
47:1120:90606:27:0:72:537:119:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Wright came to be considered as the leading modern architect for the innovative work he 
48:1121:90697:0:27:72:521:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:produced during 1890-1910, but during the next two decades he was eclipsed by a number of 
48:1122:90787:27:28:72:530:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:younger European architects, including Walter Gropius and Mies van der Rohe. By the time of 
48:1123:90879:28:27:72:528:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the Depression he had few clients, not only because of the economic climate but because, then 
48:1124:90973:27:28:72:542:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:past the age of 60, Wright was felt to be out of date. When the Pittsburgh department store owner 
48:1125:91071:28:28:72:515:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:E. J. Kaufmann approached Wright to design his weekend house near a stream at Bear Run, 
48:1126:91159:28:27:71:497:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Wright seized the opportunity to make a bold statement that would revive his career. He 
48:1127:91247:27:28:72:194:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:succeeded spectacularly. 
48:1128:91272:28:27:72:518:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Wright’s design of Fallingwater drew heavily on his own earlier buildings, including 
48:1129:91357:27:28:72:513:464:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Robie House and his own home at Taliesin. Thus the house features his trademark terraces, 
48:1130:91447:28:28:72:533:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:overhangs, rough stonework, and a variety of other features that had developed from the Prairie 
48:1131:91543:28:27:72:524:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Style. Yet true to his experimental nature, in his desire to outdo the leading European modern 
48:1132:91638:27:28:72:537:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:architects Wright was also willing to borrow their major innovations. So from the work of Mies, 
48:1133:91734:28:27:72:489:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Gropius, Le Corbusier, Schindler, and Neutra, Wright took such prominent features of 
48:1134:91819:27:28:72:536:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Fallingwater as cantilevers, extensive use of concrete and glazing, and an overall Cubist plan.209 
48:1135:91917:28:27:72:534:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Wright used these innovations, however, for his own purposes - to underscore the superiority of 
48:1136:92013:27:28:72:531:271:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:his own organic architecture over the rigidity of the severe functionalist style of the Europeans. 
48:1137:92112:28:28:72:526:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Thus a scholar recently observed that Fallingwater “used the modernist vocabulary of floating 
48:1138:92206:28:27:72:538:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:planes, but everything about it contradicted the functionalism of the style: its color, its definition 
48:1139:92309:27:28:72:533:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:by and of the landscape, its framing of vistas from within, and its metaphorical interpretation of 
48:1140:92408:28:27:72:524:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:human confrontation with nature, symbolically summed up in the stairs that descend from the 
48:1141:92500:27:28:72:520:133:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:living room to the water. Each material - stone, glass, concrete - was assigned a function, yet 
48:1142:92596:28:0:72:330:105:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:each was consonant with the site over a waterfall.”210 
49:1143:92653:0:27:72:541:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Fallingwater drew on the full experience of Wright’s five decades as an architect. He first 
49:1144:92745:27:28:72:519:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:visited Bear Run in December, 1934, but did not produce his first known plans for the house 
49:1145:92837:28:27:72:538:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:until September of the next year. Before presenting these plans to the client Wright made at least 
49:1146:92936:27:28:72:518:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:three, and perhaps four, visits to the site. In a recent study Franklin Toker concluded that the 
49:1147:93033:28:28:72:512:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:traditional story that Wright drew his first plans for Fallingwater in just a few hours, on the 
49:1148:93129:28:27:72:502:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:morning of September 22, 1935, as E. J. Kaufmann drove from Milwaukee to Taliesin, is 
49:1149:93215:27:28:72:540:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:probably a myth, and that he had likely made drawings for his own use before that date.211 Toker 
49:1150:93312:28:27:71:536:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:observed that Fallingwater contains two dramatic features that above all others made it famous - 
49:1151:93409:27:28:71:538:464:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the visual illusion that the stream actually runs through the house, and the extension of the upper 
49:1152:93509:28:28:72:533:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:balcony beyond the one below it. Toker’s study of Wright’s drawings of the plans for the house 
49:1153:93604:28:27:72:525:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:led him to conclude that one of these, the oversailing balcony, was not part of the plan Wright 
49:1154:93700:27:28:72:505:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:initially drew on September 22, but that at some point that morning “he erased its original 
49:1155:93792:28:27:72:520:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:parapet line and set a new one 19 feet farther out, which made the upper balcony oversail the 
49:1156:93886:27:28:72:533:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:living room by 6 feet.” The effect was striking: “Fallingwater now took on a totally new image, 
49:1157:93982:28:27:72:504:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:with the famous crisscross of its two main balconies.”One of Fallingwater’s most famous 
49:1158:94070:27:28:72:542:271:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:features, which “defies all structural and functional logic,” was thus an improvisation that Wright 
49:1159:94170:28:28:72:500:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:added after nine months of study of the project. Nor did Wright’s changes cease with his 
49:1160:94259:28:27:72:530:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:construction drawings. In June of 1936, for example, with construction of Fallingwater already 
49:1161:94354:27:28:72:518:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:under way, from Taliesin Wright sent new plans that changed the shape of the three massive 
49:1162:94445:28:27:71:519:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:concrete bolsters that served as the building’s main source of support - several days after the 
49:1163:94541:27:28:71:526:133:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:bolsters had been poured. Wright’s assistant who was supervising construction promptly “tore 
49:1164:94634:28:0:71:500:105:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:down the just-completed bolsters and helped construct a new set in late July. Wright was 
50:1165:94726:0:27:72:423:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:determined to give Fallingwater a thrilling profile, whatever the cost.”212 
50:1166:94801:27:28:72:530:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Fallingwater became the focus of a great flood of publicity, including feature articles in 
50:1167:94892:28:27:72:525:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:hundreds of newspapers and magazines, and an unprecedented exhibit devoted to the house at 
50:1168:94983:27:28:71:529:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:New York’s Museum of Modern Art. It quickly became “the most famous private house in the 
50:1169:95072:28:28:71:523:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:world.”213 Wright also received “the biggest PR boost of his career, and the perfect vehicle to 
50:1170:95168:28:27:72:502:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:hype his comeback,” in the form of a special issue of Architectural Forum devoted to the 
50:1171:95257:27:28:72:516:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:architect, “which has no rival as the most famous issue of any architectural magazine in any 
50:1172:95350:28:27:72:138:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:language.”214 
50:1173:95363:27:28:72:538:464:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Wright’s success was the result of producing a bold and dramatic design that synthesized 
50:1174:95452:28:28:72:533:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:major elements of his own past art with key innovations from the work of his leading European 
50:1175:95546:28:27:71:498:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:rivals, all in the service of his own organic principles: hovering over two waterfalls, and 
50:1176:95638:27:28:72:497:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:anchored among three large boulders, Fallingwater was an unmistakable example of the 
50:1177:95723:28:27:72:537:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:integration of modern architecture and nature. Approaching the age of 70, Wright produced “the 
50:1178:95818:27:28:72:541:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:most complex house of the twentieth century” through an extended and painstaking experimental 
50:1179:95912:28:27:72:476:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:process that drew on his vast working experience and mature aesthetic judgment.215 
50:1180:95994:27:28:72:535:271:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: In a recent survey of 40 textbooks of art history, two works were found to be tied for the 
50:1181:96085:28:28:71:535:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:distinction of being reproduced more often than any others made by American artists during the 
50:1182:96180:28:27:72:522:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:1980s. One of these was Tilted Arc, executed in 1981 by the sculptor Richard Serra, who was 
50:1183:96272:27:28:72:525:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:then 42 years old and widely recognized as one of the most important living American artists. 
50:1184:96366:28:27:72:532:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:The other was the Vietnam Veterans Memorial, dedicated in 1982, which had been designed by 
50:1185:96457:27:28:72:375:133:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Maya Lin at the age of 21, during her senior year in college.216 
50:1186:96521:28:0:72:512:105:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Lin originally made her design for the memorial as an assignment in an architecture 
51:1187:96608:0:27:72:525:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:seminar she took at Yale. After thinking about the purpose of the memorial, she wanted to see 
51:1188:96702:27:28:72:534:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the site, so Lin and a few friends traveled to Washington, D. C. She later recalled that “it was at 
51:1189:96802:28:27:72:303:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the site that the idea for the design took shape”: 
51:1190:96853:27:14:144:391:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: I had a simple impulse to cut into the earth. 
51:1191:96899:14:14:144:429:588:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: I imagined taking a knife and cutting into the earth, 
51:1192:96953:14:14:144:437:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:opening it up, an initial violence and pain that in time would 
51:1193:97016:14:14:143:182:560:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:heal.217 
51:1194:97024:14:27:72:539:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Lin’s plan was to have two long walls of polished black granite, arranged in a V shape, placed in 
51:1195:97122:27:28:72:532:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the ground to form an embankment. One of the walls was to point to the Lincoln Memorial, the 
51:1196:97215:28:27:72:517:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:other to the Washington Monument: “By linking these two strong symbols for the country, I 
51:1197:97305:27:28:72:540:464:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:wanted to create a unity between the country’s past and present.”218 Lin realized that the strength 
51:1198:97405:28:28:72:236:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:of her design lay in its simplicity: 
51:1199:97442:28:13:144:468:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:On our return to Yale, I quickly sketched my idea up, and it almost 
51:1200:97510:13:14:144:456:395:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:seemed too simple, too little. I toyed with adding some large flat 
51:1201:97577:14:14:144:460:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:slabs that would appear to lead into the memorial, but they didn’t 
51:1202:97644:14:14:144:471:367:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:belong. The image was so simple that anything added to it began to 
51:1203:97711:14:14:144:230:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:detract from it.219 
51:1204:97730:14:13:144:147:339:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: 
51:1205:97730:13:28:72:542:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: After Lin had completed her design, she decided to enter it in the national competition for 
51:1206:97822:28:27:72:526:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the veterans memorial. She found that the most difficult part of the entry was producing a one-
51:1207:97917:27:28:72:512:271:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:page description of the project: “It took longer, in fact, to write the statement that I felt was 
51:1208:98015:28:28:72:533:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:needed to accompany the required drawings than to design the memorial.”220 Lin explained that 
51:1209:98109:28:27:72:527:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the description was “critical to understanding the design,”  because the Memorial reflected her 
51:1210:98205:27:28:72:417:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:conceptual approach to art. Lin’s artistic goals are explicitly ideational: 
51:1211:98281:28:14:144:462:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Each of my works originates from a simple desire to make people 
51:1212:98345:14:13:144:471:146:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:aware of their surroundings, not just the physical world but also the 
51:1213:98415:13:14:144:309:133:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:psychological world we live in.221 
51:1214:98449:14:14:143:146:119:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: 
51:1215:98449:14:0:71:514:105:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:The Memorial prominently features the carved names of all the soldiers killed or missing in 
52:1216:98544:0:27:72:533:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Vietnam, reflecting Lin’s belief that “writing is the purest of art forms... Words can be the most 
52:1217:98643:27:28:72:522:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:direct means of sharing our thoughts.”222 The resemblance of the walls of the Memorial to an 
52:1218:98736:28:27:72:536:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:open book is not accidental, as Lin explained that “the memorial is analogous to a book in many 
52:1219:98832:27:28:72:354:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:ways.”223 In creating art, Lin generally begins with words: 
52:1220:98892:28:14:144:461:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: I begin by imagining an artwork verbally. I try to describe 
52:1221:98952:14:14:144:442:560:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:in writing what the project is, what it is trying to do. I need to 
52:1222:99019:14:13:144:456:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:understand the artwork without giving it a specific materiality or 
52:1223:99086:13:14:144:470:533:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:solid form. I try not to find the form too soon. Instead, I try to think 
52:1224:99159:14:14:144:327:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:about it as an idea without a shape.224 
52:1225:99198:14:14:144:147:505:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: 
52:1226:99198:14:27:72:519:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:The most important thing is to begin with a good concept: “a simple clear idea or moment of 
52:1227:99290:27:28:72:533:464:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:inspiration is the soul of the piece.” The Memorial satisfied this criterion, for it “was born of an 
52:1228:99391:28:28:72:284:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:instantaneous idea to cut open the earth.”225 
52:1229:99436:28:27:72:542:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Architectural projects are inevitably collaborative, for architects must consider the wishes 
52:1230:99529:27:28:71:542:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:of clients. Any collaboration can require compromises and deviations from an architect’s original 
52:1231:99627:28:27:72:524:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:plans, but the potential for interference with Lin’s design was enormous because of the public 
52:1232:99722:27:28:72:506:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:role of the Vietnam Veterans Memorial, and the many controversies that still surround the 
52:1233:99812:28:27:72:535:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Vietnam War. Thus even after her design was chosen by an eight-person selection committee, it 
52:1234:99906:27:28:72:538:271:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:had to go through an extended process of review by government agencies and public scrutiny, in 
52:1235:100001:28:28:72:531:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the course of which many strenuous objections were raised, by Vietnam veterans and others, to 
52:1236:100095:28:27:72:533:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the non-representational nature of Lin’s model. In an eventual compromise, a sculpture of three 
52:1237:100191:27:28:72:517:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:male soldiers was placed some distance from Lin’s monument, and later a sculpture of three 
52:1238:100282:28:27:72:539:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:female figures and a wounded soldier was also placed further away. Yet when the Memorial was 
52:1239:100375:27:28:72:505:133:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:dedicated in the fall of 1982, Lin found it did reflect her original intention: “the place was 
52:1240:100470:28:0:72:283:105:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:frighteningly close to what it should be.”226 
53:1241:100518:0:27:72:544:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Lin’s design was a radical departure from earlier memorial architecture, for the Memorial  
53:1242:100608:27:28:72:533:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:was influenced much more strongly by Minimalist sculpture than by traditional memorials. Her 
53:1243:100701:28:27:72:539:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:use of abstract forms initially shocked veterans and others who had expected a realistic portrayal 
53:1244:100800:27:28:72:521:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:of soldiers in combat, which would explicitly pay tribute to their heroism and patriotism. Yet 
53:1245:100895:28:28:72:531:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:when the Memorial was completed, it quickly came to be recognized as a moving tribute to the 
53:1246:100988:28:27:72:532:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:soldiers who had died in Vietnam. Today it is not only the most visited memorial in the capital, 
53:1247:101085:27:28:72:486:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:but it is widely considered to have established a new level of excellence for memorial 
53:1248:101172:28:27:72:506:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:architecture. So for example when the Lower Manhattan Development Corporation held a 
53:1249:101257:27:28:72:530:464:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:competition for a memorial to the victims of the 2001 attack on the World Trade Center, Maya 
53:1250:101350:28:28:72:528:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Lin was appointed to the five member jury. When the eight final designs were presented to the 
53:1251:101444:28:27:72:503:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:public, the architecture critic for the New Yorker remarked that although all of these were 
53:1252:101536:27:28:72:511:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:intelligent and sophisticated, they received a lukewarm reaction from critics and the public 
53:1253:101629:28:27:72:500:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:because “in the post-Vietnam-memorial age, we may have come to expect too much of a 
53:1254:101713:27:28:72:531:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:memorial.” The problem was that Lin had set a new standard: “Lin’s Vietnam memorial set the 
53:1255:101805:28:27:72:159:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:bar very high.”227 
53:1256:101823:27:28:72:540:271:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: In the two decades since she designed the Vietnam Veterans Memorial, Lin has pursued a 
53:1257:101910:28:28:72:534:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:career as a architect and sculptor. A recent profile observed that “Now a beneficiary of a stream 
53:1258:102008:28:27:72:528:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:of commissions, this still-young master is riding her good fortune, turning out institutional and 
53:1259:102106:27:28:72:491:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:private projects while also making the individual sculptures to which she attaches such 
53:1260:102194:28:27:72:524:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:importance.”228 Yet the survey of textbooks found no other work by Lin reproduced in even a 
53:1261:102286:27:28:72:539:133:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:single book.229 Thus from the vantage point of art scholars Lin’s contribution consists of a single 
53:1262:102386:28:0:71:506:105:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:work, that one scholar describes as “one of the most compelling monuments in the United 
54:1263:102477:0:27:72:532:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:States.”230 That a 21-year-old artist could conceive an idea that would be fully expressed in one 
54:1264:102575:27:28:72:528:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:enormously successful project, and that would be followed by no others deemed significant by 
54:1265:102668:28:27:71:539:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:art scholars, is a quintessentially conceptual phenomenon. Unlike the aging Frank Lloyd Wright, 
54:1266:102764:27:28:71:540:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:who worked surrounded by assistants and apprentices at an academy dedicated to making his art, 
54:1267:102859:28:28:71:539:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the young Maya Lin worked alone: the Vietnam Veterans Memorial was first given solid form in 
54:1268:102952:28:27:71:519:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:mashed potatoes at her college dining hall.231 And unlike Wright’s extended and painstaking 
54:1269:103044:27:28:71:536:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:revisions, the Memorial “was born of an instantaneous idea.”232 These features of Lin’s method, 
54:1270:103140:28:27:71:493:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:and the success of her design, may all have been consequences of her youth and lack of 
54:1271:103227:27:28:71:517:464:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:experience. As one of the jurors for the competition commented on seeing Lin’s unorthodox 
54:1272:103317:28:28:71:517:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:entry, the architect “must really know what he is doing to dare to do something so naive.”233 
54:1273:103410:28:27:71:154:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Movie Directors 
54:1274:103425:27:14:144:430:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Q: During the shooting [of Citizen Kane], did you have the 
54:1275:103484:14:14:144:361:367:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:sensation of making such an important film? 
54:1276:103528:14:14:144:367:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Welles: I never doubted it for a single instant. 
54:1277:103577:14:13:324:469:339:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Interview with Orson Welles, 
54:1278:103606:13:14:324:363:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:1964234 
54:1279:103613:14:14:144:147:312:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: 
54:1280:103613:14:14:144:448:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:I do think that there is an art to the making of a motion picture. 
54:1281:103680:14:13:144:462:284:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:There are some great artists in the business. I am not one of them. 
54:1282:103748:13:14:144:417:271:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:                                                            John            Ford,            1973235 
54:1283:103848:14:14:144:147:257:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: 
54:1284:103848:14:28:72:523:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:There is remarkably widespread agreement that Citizen Kane is the most important American 
54:1285:103938:28:27:72:522:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:movie ever made. Thus for example Citizen Kane ranked first in a “definitive selection of the 
54:1286:104032:27:28:72:537:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:100 greatest American movies of all time,” as determined by a poll of more than 1,500 members 
54:1287:104126:28:27:72:528:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f5:of the American film community conducted in 2000 by the American Film Institute.236 Citizen 
54:1288:104217:27:28:71:515:133:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:Kane also placed first in a ranking of the 100 best films of the 20th century compiled by The 
54:1289:104311:28:0:71:495:105:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f4:Village Voice from a poll the newspaper conducted of 50 distinguished film critics. The 
55:1290:104402:0:27:72:542:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:screenplay for Citizen Kane similarly ranked first in a 2001 survey of the members of the Writers 
55:1291:104500:27:28:72:523:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Guild of America.237 Nor is Kane’s fame limited to the United States. Once every decade, the 
55:1292:104593:28:27:72:521:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:British film magazine Sight & Sound conducts an international poll of critics and directors to 
55:1293:104688:27:28:72:510:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:determine the 10 best movies ever made. Citizen Kane placed first in this poll in 1962, and 
55:1294:104780:28:28:71:504:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:repeated this success in every subsequent decennial poll, including the most recent one in 
55:1295:104871:28:27:71:531:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:2002.238 When Sight & Sound recently reprinted a paperback edition of Pauline Kael’s book on 
55:1296:104964:27:28:72:524:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the making of Citizen Kane, titled Raising Kane, the only print on the book’s front cover read 
55:1297:105059:28:27:71:538:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:“Pauline Kael on the best film ever made.”239 Francois Truffaut recalled the enormous impact of 
55:1298:105155:27:28:72:529:464:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f4:Citizen Kane: “This film has inspired more vocations to cinema throughout the world than any 
55:1299:105248:28:28:72:501:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:other.”240 Among the most celebrated facts about Citizen Kane is that it was directed and 
55:1300:105338:28:27:72:538:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:coauthored by the boy-wonder Orson Welles, who also played the title role, when he was just 25 
55:1301:105433:27:28:72:242:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:years old. It was Welles’ first film. 
55:1302:105471:28:27:72:536:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: The importance of Citizen Kane derived in large part from its technical virtuosity. So for 
55:1303:105562:27:28:72:392:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:example a recent survey of film history explained its contribution: 
55:1304:105630:28:14:144:447:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:It enabled the spectator not only to look through the frame at a 
55:1305:105695:14:13:144:459:284:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:make-believe world, but to see once again, so to speak, the frame 
55:1306:105761:13:14:144:455:271:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:as a constructed image... [N]o single aspect of Citizen Kane was 
55:1307:105826:14:14:144:429:257:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:entirely original or unknown to filmmakers, but the work’s 
55:1308:105885:14:14:144:438:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:startling impact came from its total effect, the concentration, 
55:1309:105949:14:14:144:466:229:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:comprehensiveness, and unity of its stylistic effort... Welles strove 
55:1310:106019:14:13:144:443:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:with his collaborators to utilize multiple innovations in nearly 
55:1311:106084:13:14:144:390:202:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:every shot and scene throughout the whole film.241 
55:1312:106134:14:14:144:147:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: 
55:1313:106134:14:28:72:515:174:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f4:Citizen Kane’s technical sophistication was not accidental, but was a result of exceptionally 
55:1314:106228:28:27:72:513:146:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:careful planning. Both the film’s composer and its photographer emphasized that they were 
55:1315:106318:27:0:72:510:119:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:given exceptional amounts of time to plan and achieve the novel aims they and Welles had 
56:1316:106410:0:27:72:524:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:formulated. Thus Bernard Herrmann wrote that he and Wells agreed that “the dynamics of all 
56:1317:106501:27:28:72:507:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:music in the picture should be planned ahead of time.” Contrary to the normal Hollywood 
56:1318:106589:28:27:72:537:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:procedure in which musical scores were not written until filming was completed, Herrmann was 
56:1319:106682:27:28:72:542:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:given time to write his score before filming began, and was then allowed to work on the film as it 
56:1320:106781:28:28:72:539:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:was being shot and edited. In a number of scenes, film sequences were actually tailored to match 
56:1321:106878:28:27:72:530:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the music. Herrmann observed of the completed movie that “the result is an exact projection of 
56:1322:106973:27:28:72:516:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the original ideas in the score.”242 Similarly, Gregg Toland explained that “the photographic 
56:1323:107067:28:27:72:536:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:approach to Citizen Kane was planned and considered long before the first camera turned.” This 
56:1324:107162:27:28:72:534:464:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:allowed Toland time not only to formulate novel plans, but to make extensive experiments with 
56:1325:107256:28:28:72:507:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:equipment and sets to make the plans possible. In this he had Welles’ full support: “Orson 
56:1326:107347:28:27:72:540:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Welles was insistent that the story be told most effectively, letting the Hollywood conventions of 
56:1327:107446:27:28:72:488:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:movie-making go hang if need be.” Toland credited Welles for the opportunity: “Such 
56:1328:107530:28:27:72:521:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:differences as exist between the cinematography in Citizen Kane and the camera work on the 
56:1329:107621:27:28:72:520:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:average Hollywood product are based on the rare opportunity provided me by Orson Welles, 
56:1330:107710:28:27:72:518:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:who was in complete sympathy with my theory that the photography should fit the story.”243 
56:1331:107800:27:28:72:542:271:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: The meticulous planning of Welles and his collaborators produced a movie that contained 
56:1332:107888:28:28:72:532:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:many innovations involving both sound and sight. A number of the sound innovations reflected 
56:1333:107981:28:27:72:541:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Welles’ earlier experience in radio. These included musical bridges - the introduction of music in 
56:1334:108080:27:28:72:540:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the middle of a scene, to change the mood and foreshadow the transition to the next scene; sound 
56:1335:108177:28:27:72:536:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:montages - series of short bursts of speech, that revealed the reactions of a number of characters 
56:1336:108276:27:28:72:515:133:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:in quick succession; and overlapping dialogue tracks that mimicked the interruptions of real 
56:1337:108369:28:0:72:521:105:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:conversation, with variation in sound levels that allowed one voice to be heard at a time. The 
57:1338:108467:0:27:72:519:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:visual innovations in Citizen Kane have become even more famous. A number of these were 
57:1339:108555:27:28:72:514:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:used to attain what Toland called “human-eye focus,” with much greater depth of field than 
57:1340:108646:28:27:72:479:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:movies normally afforded. Contributing to this was the staging, with construction of 
57:1341:108731:27:28:72:541:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:exceptionally deep sets, so the action of a scene could occur simultaneously at different distances 
57:1342:108831:28:28:72:528:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:from the camera; the use of extremely wide-angle lenses, with high-speed films, and very high 
57:1343:108925:28:27:72:515:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:levels of illumination, which allowed sharp focus throughout the deep space of the sets, and 
57:1344:109018:27:28:72:533:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:often created the startling effect of having important action in the background; and long camera 
57:1345:109115:28:27:72:530:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:takes that allowed greater freedom of movement and extended ensemble acting for the players. 
57:1346:109208:27:28:72:494:464:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:The greater realism produced by the novel device of building ceilings over the sets also 
57:1347:109297:28:28:72:521:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:permitted the dramatic low-angle shots that became one of the movie’s technical trademarks. 
57:1348:109389:28:27:72:526:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Citizen Kane became celebrated for its many innovative technical devices, but Welles’ 
57:1349:109475:27:28:72:531:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:greatest achievement probably lay in the integration of these many devices in the service of the 
57:1350:109572:28:27:72:541:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:film’s story.244 The dramatic use of chiaroscuro in lighting, the fragmentation of the film’s action 
57:1351:109673:27:28:72:539:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:in physical depth, staccato bursts of spoken words, and many other technical effects all served to 
57:1352:109772:28:27:72:497:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:underscore the symbolic content of the film. Jorge Luis Borges recognized this when he 
57:1353:109859:27:28:72:500:271:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:observed that Citizen’s Kane’s subject is “the discovery of the secret soul of a man,” and 
57:1354:109950:28:28:72:541:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:explained that “In astonishing and endlessly varied ways, Orson Welles exhibits the fragments of 
57:1355:110047:28:27:71:541:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the life of the man, Charles Foster Kane, and invites us to combine and reconstruct them.”245 The 
57:1356:110145:27:28:72:533:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:variety of technical means used to tell the story parallels the variety of views of Kane presented 
57:1357:110244:28:27:72:524:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:by different characters, which evolved from the original idea motivating the film: thus Welles 
57:1358:110339:27:28:72:534:133:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:recalled that the story of Kane began with “the idea of telling the same thing several times - and 
57:1359:110438:28:0:72:500:105:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:showing exactly the same scene from wholly different points of view. Basically, the idea 
58:1360:110530:0:27:72:210:684:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f4:Rashomon used later on.”246 
58:1361:110557:27:28:72:505:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Welles’ conceptual approach to making movies is reflected in his emphasis on the 
58:1362:110638:28:27:72:540:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:primacy of dialogue over images or action. Thus in a 1964 interview he declared: “I know that in 
58:1363:110735:27:28:72:531:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:theory the word is secondary in cinema but the secret of my work is that everything is based on 
58:1364:110831:28:28:72:517:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the word. I do not make silent films. I must begin with what the characters say. I must know 
58:1365:110924:28:27:72:530:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:what they say before seeing them do what they do.”247 For Welles, a good script was necessary 
58:1366:111018:27:28:71:499:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:for a good film: “I’m sure I can’t make good films unless I also write the screenplay.”248 
58:1367:111108:28:27:71:525:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Citizen Kane is a conceptual masterpiece, a great early work executed by an important 
58:1368:111194:27:28:71:512:464:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:conceptual innovator. It dominates Welles’ career. Thus Gerald Mast observed that “unlike 
58:1369:111284:28:28:71:513:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Hitchcock, Lubitsch, Chaplin, Hawks, or Ford, whose reputations rest on a great number of 
58:1370:111374:28:27:71:536:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:impressive films, critical respect for Orson Welles rests primarily on one film, Citizen Kane.”249 
58:1371:111472:27:28:72:541:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Andrew Sarris stressed the allegorical nature of the film: “Kane develops two interesting themes: 
58:1372:111570:28:27:72:502:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the debasement of the private personality of the public figure, and the crushing weight of 
58:1373:111661:27:28:72:536:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:materialism. Taken together, these two themes comprise the bitter irony of an American success 
58:1374:111756:28:27:72:522:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:story that ends in futile nostalgia, loneliness, and death.”250 Francois Truffaut recognized that 
58:1375:111854:27:28:72:536:271:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Welles had achieved what all young directors hope to do: “To shoot Citizen Kane at twenty-five 
58:1376:111949:28:28:71:485:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:years of age, is this not the dream of all the young habitués of the cinematheques?”251 
58:1377:112036:28:27:72:540:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: A great deal of critical energy has been devoted to explaining how a young director could 
58:1378:112126:27:28:72:537:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:produce such a great masterpiece as his first movie. Although Welles had no prior experience as 
58:1379:112222:28:27:72:504:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:a film director, he had behind him a great deal of experience, and success, as an actor and 
58:1380:112314:27:28:72:524:133:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:director in the theater and radio: as Truffaut put it, Kane is “the only first film made by a man 
58:1381:112412:28:0:72:534:105:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:who was already famous.” For Truffaut, the movie bore witness to Welles’ iconoclasm: “Wells, 
59:1382:112508:0:27:72:502:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:with extraordinary arrogance, had rejected the rules of cinema, the limits of its powers of 
59:1383:112600:27:28:72:527:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:illusion.”252 Citizen Kane drew liberally on the expertise Welles had acquired in the other arts. 
59:1384:112698:28:27:71:530:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Peter Bogdanovich reflected that “Citizen Kane is like watching a consummate artist grappling 
59:1385:112792:27:28:71:524:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:for the first time with the intoxication of his found vocation. All his passions - theatre, magic, 
59:1386:112891:28:28:71:524:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:circus, radio, painting, literature - suddenly fused into one... No other director discovering the 
59:1387:112990:28:27:71:520:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:medium was as ready or as mature.”253 Pauline Kael stressed the importance of an attitude in 
59:1388:113083:27:28:71:542:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Welles that Bernard Herrmann and Gregg Toland had both described: “He was young and open... 
59:1389:113175:28:27:72:524:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Welles was so eager to try out new ideas that even the tough, hardened studio craftsmen were 
59:1390:113268:27:28:71:521:464:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:caught up by his spirit, just as his co-workers in the theatre and in radio had been.”254 Welles 
59:1391:113365:28:28:72:522:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:himself had a slightly different explanation. When asked where he’d gotten the confidence to 
59:1392:113458:28:27:72:518:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:make such a major effort so young, he replied: “Ignorance, ignorance, sheer ignorance - you 
59:1393:113550:27:28:72:538:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:know there’s no confidence to equal it. It’s only when you know something about a profession, I 
59:1394:113646:28:27:72:255:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:think, that you’re timid or careful.”255 
59:1395:113686:27:28:72:530:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Many movie critics consider John Ford to have been a great director. In 1973, when the 
59:1396:113773:28:27:72:524:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:American Film Institute established its Life Achievement Award to honor individuals “whose 
59:1397:113864:27:28:72:532:271:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:talent has, in a fundamental way, advanced the film art, and whose accomplishments have been 
59:1398:113957:28:28:72:523:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:acknowledged by scholars, critics, professional peers, and the general public,” the first award 
59:1399:114053:28:27:72:532:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:was given to Ford. The Institute’s citation declared that “No individual has more fully explored 
59:1400:114150:27:28:72:529:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:on film the American experience.”256 Ford has been the subject of monographs not only by the 
59:1401:114243:28:27:72:500:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:distinguished critic Andrew Sarris, but also by the directors Lindsay Anderson and Peter 
59:1402:114332:27:28:72:542:133:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Bogdanovich. Anderson considered that Ford was “probably the greatest film director working in 
59:1403:114427:28:0:71:525:105:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the world’s richest film making tradition.” 257When Orson Welles was asked which American 
60:1404:114520:0:27:72:528:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:directors he most admired, he replied “the old masters. By which I mean John Ford, John Ford 
60:1405:114613:27:28:72:164:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:and John Ford.”258 
60:1406:114631:28:27:72:536:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Ford directed more than 140 movies, and won six Oscars. Curiously, however, no one of 
60:1407:114717:27:28:72:520:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:his movies has emerged clearly as a masterpiece. No Ford film was ranked among the top 20 
60:1408:114807:28:28:72:519:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:American movies of all time in the American Film Institute’s survey conducted in 2000, and 
60:1409:114898:28:27:72:501:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:only three of his films were ranked in the top 100. The Institute’s citation for Ford’s Life 
60:1410:114991:27:28:72:518:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Achievement Award did not mention any specific movie, but instead referred collectively to 
60:1411:115082:28:27:72:519:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Ford’s films as “a creative tapestry representing over 50 years of work.”259 Although there is 
60:1412:115177:27:28:72:526:464:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:considerable disagreement even among Ford’s admirers over what constitutes his best work, a 
60:1413:115269:28:28:72:533:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:number of experts have named The Searchers as his greatest achievement. So for example John 
60:1414:115361:28:27:72:526:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Baxter called it “Ford’s most perfect philosophical statement,” and Gerald Peary considered it 
60:1415:115456:27:28:72:531:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:“the pinnacle of Ford’s cinematic accomplishment.”260 Ford directed The Searchers in 1956, at 
60:1416:115550:28:27:72:155:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the age of 62.261  
60:1417:115569:27:28:72:539:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: That Ford may have been a master without a masterpiece and that his work was excellent 
60:1418:115656:28:27:72:532:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:late in his career both appear to have been consequences of the fact that his approach to art was 
60:1419:115754:27:28:72:539:271:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:experimental. Ford’s work is consistently praised for its visual qualities. Alfred Hitchcock stated 
60:1420:115854:28:28:72:543:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:that “A John Ford film was a visual gratification.”262 Elia Kazan declared that Ford “taught me to 
60:1421:115953:28:27:71:517:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:tell it in pictures.”263 Orson Welles made a similar statement when asked how he learned his 
60:1422:116046:27:28:72:133:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:visual style: 
60:1423:116060:28:14:144:444:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:I’ve only been influenced by somebody once: prior to making 
60:1424:116120:14:13:144:461:146:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f4:Citizen Kane I saw [Ford’s] Stagecoach forty times. I didn’t need 
60:1425:116186:13:14:143:437:133:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:to learn from somebody who had something to say, but from 
60:1426:116244:14:14:143:450:119:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:somebody who would show me how to say what I had in mind; 
60:1427:116302:14:0:143:316:105:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:and John Ford is perfect for that.264 
61:1428:116342:0:13:144:147:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: 
61:1429:116342:13:28:72:515:671:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Federico Fellini stressed Ford’s direct appeal to another one of the senses: “When I think of 
61:1430:116436:28:28:71:382:643:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Ford, I sense the smell of barracks, of horses, of gunpowder.”265 
61:1431:116501:28:27:72:538:615:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Ford’s films are known for their stories and for ensemble acting. Thus a recent history of 
61:1432:116592:27:28:72:538:588:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:film cited Ford as “a good example of the studio director who defined himself over a long career 
61:1433:116689:28:27:72:538:560:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:by way of story and performance. It is possible to speak of a kind of Fordian world... peopled by 
61:1434:116787:27:28:72:529:533:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:a repertory group of players.”266 Unlike Welles, Ford did not consider the script to be a critical 
61:1435:116886:28:28:71:530:505:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:determinant of the quality of a movie. Thus he explained that “After all, you’ve got to tell your 
61:1436:116984:28:27:72:521:477:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:story through the people who portray it. You can have a weak, utterly bad script - and a good 
61:1437:117078:27:28:72:529:450:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:cast will turn it into a good picture.”267 Gerald Mast observed that “Ford’s method emphasized 
61:1438:117173:28:27:72:539:422:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:visual images rather than talk,” and Ford agreed, stating that “Pictures, not words, should tell the 
61:1439:117274:27:28:72:394:395:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:story.”268 On another occasion Ford elaborated on his philosophy:  
61:1440:117341:28:14:144:459:367:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:When a motion picture is at its best, it is long on action and short 
61:1441:117410:14:14:144:456:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:on dialogue. When it tells its story and reveals its characters in a 
61:1442:117479:14:13:144:467:339:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:series of simple, beautiful, active pictures, and does it with as little 
61:1443:117552:13:14:144:458:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:talk as possible, then the motion picture medium is being used to 
61:1444:117618:14:14:144:258:312:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:its fullest advantage.269 
61:1445:117643:14:14:144:147:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: 
61:1446:117643:14:27:72:531:284:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Ford’s goal was to achieve immediacy and realism: “I try to make people forget they’re 
61:1447:117730:27:28:72:533:257:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:in a theatre. I don’t want them to be conscious of a camera or a screen. I want them to feel what 
61:1448:117828:28:27:72:528:229:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:they’re seeing is real.”270 He distrusted not only extensive dialogue but also complex technical 
61:1449:117925:27:28:72:522:202:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:devices: “I like, as a director and a spectator, simple, direct, frank films. Nothing disgusts me 
61:1450:118023:28:28:71:504:174:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:more than snobbism, mannerism, technical gratuity... and, most of all, intellectualism.”271 
61:1451:118114:28:27:71:507:146:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Lindsay Anderson remarked that Ford achieved a wide range of emotional effects through 
61:1452:118201:27:0:71:524:119:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:technical mastery, but that he never allowed technique to obtrude on narrative: “Ford remains 
62:1453:118298:0:27:72:192:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:always a story-teller.”272 
62:1454:118324:27:28:72:470:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Although Ford began directing movies at the age of 23, his early work was 
62:1455:118398:28:27:72:537:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:undistinguished. Thus Andrew Sarris commented that if Ford’s career had ended in 1929 - when 
62:1456:118491:27:28:72:541:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:he was 35, and had already directed more than 65 films - “he would deserve at most a footnote in 
62:1457:118588:28:28:72:524:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:film history.”273 Like that of other experimental artists, Ford’s work developed gradually, and 
62:1458:118684:28:27:72:538:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:with considerably continuity: Peter Bogdanovich remarked that “Every Ford movie is filled with 
62:1459:118779:27:28:72:538:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:reverberations from another - which makes his use of the same players from year to year, decade 
62:1460:118875:28:27:72:538:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:to decade, so much more than just building ‘a stock company’ - and one film of his cannot really 
62:1461:118972:27:28:72:532:464:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:be looked at as separate from the rest.”274 Ford is widely considered to have improved his work 
62:1462:119068:28:28:72:507:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:until late in his life. Andrew Sarris judged that “the last two decades of his career were his 
62:1463:119163:28:27:72:525:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:richest and most rewarding.”275 Similarly, Peter Bogdanovich considered Ford’s late films his 
62:1464:119257:27:28:72:355:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:best, “not only in execution but in depth of expression.”276 
62:1465:119317:28:27:72:540:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: The explanation of why Ford’s work improved as he aged may be the same as the answer 
62:1466:119402:27:28:72:531:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:he himself gave when asked how he chose where to place his cameras: “You shoot what would 
62:1467:119492:28:27:72:501:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f5:look best on the screen. Experience, instinct. That’s it.”277 Andrew Sarris considered The 
62:1468:119583:27:28:72:515:271:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f4:Searchers a stylistic summation of “all the best of what Ford had been,” and emphasized its 
62:1469:119675:28:28:72:542:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:beauty: “The Searchers is rich in all the colors and textures of the seasons and the elements, from 
62:1470:119775:28:27:72:538:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the whiteness of winter snows to the brownness of summer sands.”278 Sarris believed that Ford’s 
62:1471:119871:27:28:72:514:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:experience was the key to his late achievements: “The economy of expression that Ford has 
62:1472:119961:28:27:72:440:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:achieved in fifty years of film-making constitutes the beauty of his style.”279 
62:1473:120040:27:28:72:237:133:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Young Geniuses and Old Masters 
62:1474:120070:28:0:144:436:105:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:There is, it seems, a graph of creativity which can be plotted 
63:1475:120136:0:13:144:270:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:through an artist’s career. 
63:1476:120164:13:14:144:455:671:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:                                                            Sir            Alan            Bowness,            1989280 
63:1477:120282:14:14:144:147:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: 
63:1478:120282:14:28:72:523:643:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: This consideration of important contributions made either very early or very late in an 
63:1479:120370:28:27:72:536:615:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:artist’s career in seven different artistic disciplines demonstrates not only that there are dramatic 
63:1480:120472:27:28:72:527:588:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:differences in basic characteristics of the work of conceptual and experimental innovators, but 
63:1481:120568:28:27:72:511:560:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:also that there are significant similarities within each of these categories across disciplines. 
63:1482:120665:27:28:71:503:533:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:            Conceptual            innovators            historically have been those artists most often described as 
63:1483:120782:28:28:71:500:505:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:geniuses, as their early manifestations of brilliance have been taken to indicate that these 
63:1484:120875:28:27:71:520:477:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:individuals were born with extraordinary talents. Conceptual innovators normally make their 
63:1485:120967:27:28:71:529:450:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:most important contributions to a discipline not long after their first exposure to it. These early 
63:1486:121067:28:27:71:527:422:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:innovators are often perceived as irreverent and iconoclastic. Among the cases examined here, 
63:1487:121161:27:28:71:540:395:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Kosuth, Rimbaud, Boccioni, and Jarry offer examples of artists whose lack of respect for, or lack 
63:1488:121259:28:28:71:527:367:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:of interest in, earlier work in their disciplines figured prominently in their ability to make bold 
63:1489:121359:28:27:71:536:339:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:new departures from existing practices. Conceptual innovations are often very simple. Although 
63:1490:121454:27:28:71:507:312:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Kosuth, Boccioni, and Lin had not spent long periods of time acquiring the complex skills 
63:1491:121544:28:27:71:535:284:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:common to many practitioners of their disciplines, the radical simplifications they made in their 
63:1492:121642:27:28:71:542:257:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:art allowed them to avoid the need for those skills. Kosuth, Rimbaud, Boccioni, Jarry, and Lin all 
63:1493:121741:28:27:71:540:229:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:shared the extremely rapid formation of ideas that characterizes many conceptual innovations, as 
63:1494:121838:27:28:71:498:202:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the central elements of their major contributions arrived in brief moments of inspiration. 
63:1495:121929:28:28:71:508:174:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Conceptual innovations often involve radical leaps, producing work that not only does not 
63:1496:122019:28:27:71:540:146:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:resemble other artists’ work, but equally does not resemble the innovator’s own earlier work. All 
63:1497:122117:27:0:71:536:119:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:seven major conceptual innovations considered here share this characteristic, as in each case the 
64:1498:122218:0:27:72:530:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:specific work examined marked a sharp discontinuity in the career of the artist. A consequence 
64:1499:122313:27:28:72:519:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:of the sudden declaration of conceptual innovations together with their radical nature is their 
64:1500:122409:28:27:72:525:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:frequent landmark status. In six of the seven cases considered here, the work examined in this 
64:1501:122504:27:28:72:495:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:paper clearly dominates the innovator’s career. Thus the mention of Kosuth, Fitzgerald, 
64:1502:122592:28:28:72:522:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Boccioni, Jarry, Lin, or Welles immediately brings to mind a single trademark work. Perhaps 
64:1503:122684:28:27:72:529:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:most fundamentally, this examination of seven major conceptual contributions underscores the 
64:1504:122777:27:28:72:533:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:certainty of these important conceptual innovators. All seven of the artists had great confidence 
64:1505:122875:28:27:72:538:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:in the validity and significance of their innovations, and this allowed them to put forward radical 
64:1506:122975:27:28:72:482:464:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:contributions early in their careers in spite of their knowledge that many, if not most, 
64:1507:123064:28:28:72:377:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:practitioners of their disciplines would be hostile to their ideas. 
64:1508:123132:28:27:72:529:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: Experimental innovators are most often praised for their wisdom and judgment. All the 
64:1509:123218:27:28:72:470:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:experimental innovations examined here are considered prime examples of superb 
64:1510:123297:28:27:72:539:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:craftsmanship, the result of experience acquired over the course of long careers by their creators. 
64:1511:123397:27:28:72:527:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:All seven experimental innovators considered here are celebrated for their deep understanding 
64:1512:123491:28:27:72:526:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:and respect for the traditions of their disciplines. With the exception of Wright’s Fallingwater, 
64:1513:123589:27:28:72:520:271:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:the major works considered here were not intended as definitive statements, but were instead 
64:1514:123682:28:28:72:539:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:provisional, subject to later modification or further development, reflecting their author’s lack of 
64:1515:123783:28:27:72:485:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:certainty in their accomplishment. It is this uncertainty that is the most basic common 
64:1516:123871:27:28:72:536:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:characteristic of these great experimental innovators. Bishop, Rodin, Ibsen, Wright, and Ford all 
64:1517:123969:28:27:72:506:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:continued beyond the specific contributions examined here, progressively modifying their 
64:1518:124058:27:28:72:516:133:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:innovations in later works through further experimentation; Mondrian and Dostoevsky were 
64:1519:124147:28:0:72:522:105:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:prevented from doing this only by death. The work of these experimental innovators not only 
65:1520:124242:0:27:72:489:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:makes explicit statements of uncertainty and ambiguity, but in some cases has implicit 
65:1521:124329:27:28:72:518:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:expressions of uncertainty built into its fabric. Notable examples of this include the irregular 
65:1522:124426:28:27:72:538:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:brushstrokes of Mondrian’s late paintings and Dostoevsky’s innovation of the polyphonic novel. 
65:1523:124521:27:28:72:488:602:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: This paper’s examination of seven major conceptual innovators has interesting 
65:1524:124599:28:28:72:523:574:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:implications for a familiar problem that has previously been considered almost exclusively in 
65:1525:124693:28:27:72:540:546:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:relation to one artist at a time, of why some important artists decline precipitously after making a 
65:1526:124794:27:28:72:529:519:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:great early contribution. Some conceptual artists become tied to an early important innovation, 
65:1527:124890:28:27:72:516:491:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:and produce later work that effectively repeats it in subject or technique. Jarry is an extreme 
65:1528:124986:27:28:72:516:464:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:example of an artist who became the captive of his early achievement, but to a lesser degree 
65:1529:125079:28:28:72:532:436:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:Kosuth, Lin, and Welles all revisited their early innovations in their later work. In some cases a 
65:1530:125178:28:27:72:540:408:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:conceptual innovator loses the power of his early approach by aiming to produce later works that 
65:1531:125275:27:28:72:541:381:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:are more complex. Kosuth and Lin have both made later contributions that are more involved but 
65:1532:125370:28:27:72:531:353:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:less influential than their early masterpieces, and the failure of Tender is the Night to match the 
65:1533:125470:27:28:72:540:326:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:importance of The Great Gatsby is probably due to Fitzgerald’s attempt to write a more complex 
65:1534:125565:28:27:72:511:298:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:novel. In each of these cases, the artist’s decline appears to have been a consequence of the 
65:1535:125659:27:28:72:505:271:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:failure to recognize that the key to the success of an early landmark contribution lay in its 
65:1536:125753:28:28:72:535:243:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:simplicity. In yet other cases, a brilliant conceptual innovator may lose interest in his discipline. 
65:1537:125855:28:27:72:530:215:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:It is often difficult to determine whether this plays a role in the career of a particular innovator, 
65:1538:125957:27:28:72:531:188:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:but among the most dramatic instances of it is surely Rimbaud’s definitive decision to abandon 
65:1539:126052:28:27:72:504:160:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:poetry            at            the            age            of            19.                                                                                                            
65:1540:126239:27:28:72:535:133:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4: This paper clearly demonstrates the generality of the distinction between conceptual and 
65:1541:126328:28:0:72:522:105:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:experimental innovators in artistic disciplines. In a wide range of very different activities it is 
66:1542:126431:0:27:72:533:684:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:readily apparent that some artists are conceptual, and others experimental. Examination of their 
66:1543:126528:27:28:72:485:657:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:contributions furthermore allows us to understand why it is that important conceptual 
66:1544:126614:28:0:72:531:629:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:innovations are generally made by the young, and major experimental contributions by the old.
